<div id="review_104219101" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/104219101" />
    <a title="Julia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1313520-julia"><img alt="Julia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1257953885p2/1313520.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/104219101?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julia" href="/user/show/1313520-julia">Julia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1313520-julia?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1313520-julia?shelf=appropriate-for-high-school">appropriate-for-high-school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1313520-julia?shelf=appropriate-for-middle-school">appropriate-for-middle-school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1313520-julia?shelf=romance-dating">romance-dating</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1313520-julia?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer104219101" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10303127914749588648">This book is readable & will probably appeal to some teens. That makes me sad.<br/><br/>Sorry to those of you who liked it, but this book has more flaws than I can count. The premise of a girl with a supernatural ability to sense (hear, smell, see, etc.) murder victims and their killers was a cool one. The problem is that the mystery had flaws. It was not solvable by the reader - despite reading occasional mini-chapters from the killer's point of view - because the reader doesn't really meet the killer an</span>
  <span id="freeText10303127914749588648" style="display:none">This book is readable &amp; will probably appeal to some teens. That makes me sad.<br /><br />Sorry to those of you who liked it, but this book has more flaws than I can count. The premise of a girl with a supernatural ability to sense (hear, smell, see, etc.) murder victims and their killers was a cool one. The problem is that the mystery had flaws. It was not solvable by the reader - despite reading occasional mini-chapters from the killer's point of view - because the reader doesn't really meet the killer anywhere else. That made it a huge let down after building suspense around every other male in the book.<br /><br />However, where I give the mystery a C+, I have to give the romance in the book a C- or maybe even a D. There was no originality or suspense. Girl discovers she suddenly has feelings for best friend (a boy). She tries to supress it so the friendship isn't ruined. But anyone with half a brain can see that he likes her too. Her stupidity can be forgiven due to teenage insecurities/blindness. However, once they get together the dialogue about their feelings is generic romance novel stuff. Blech. Not to mention that the boyfriend is incredibly vanilla "perfect guy." <br /><br />Plus one last observation: any book that has a scene where the girl is racing away from the killer &amp; actually trips &amp; falls only to be saved by the spontaneous appearance of her boyfriend just screams cheap (and sexist) theatrics. Sadly, someone will probably make a movie of this unworthy book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10303127914749588648" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11879579001989962193" style="display:none">What the hell? Why is this book rated so highly? All I read was a boring and undeveloped typical YA PNR. <div id="review_103795079" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/103795079" />
    <a title="Lindsay" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3721849-lindsay"><img alt="Lindsay" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1319938182p2/3721849.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/103795079?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsay" href="/user/show/3721849-lindsay">Lindsay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3721849-lindsay?shelf=heart-pounding">heart-pounding</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3721849-lindsay?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3721849-lindsay?shelf=cover-lust">cover-lust</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3721849-lindsay?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer103795079" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11014643950188877887"><a href='http://imlovingbooks.com/freebies/mini-series-banners' title='The Body Finder by Kimberly Derting' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379768825i/272107.jpg' alt='The Body Finder by Kimberly Derting' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>You know, books like these really make me stop and ask book lovers like myself a really important question. WHY OH WHY DID IT TAKE ME SO LONG TO READ THIS? SERIOUSLY! This book has been sitting on my shelf now for months. I remember it being on my to-read list for god knows how long and how excited I was to read it but after I bought it, I just didn't pick it up again. And now that I have read it...I have to say that I am amazed!<br/><br/>I mean, when I first started reading this, my rating for the bo</span>
  <span id="freeText11014643950188877887" style="display:none"><a href="http://imlovingbooks.com/freebies/mini-series-banners" title="The Body Finder by Kimberly Derting" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379768825i/272107.jpg" alt="The Body Finder by Kimberly Derting" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>You know, books like these really make me stop and ask book lovers like myself a really important question. WHY OH WHY DID IT TAKE ME SO LONG TO READ THIS? SERIOUSLY! This book has been sitting on my shelf now for months. I remember it being on my to-read list for god knows how long and how excited I was to read it but after I bought it, I just didn't pick it up again. And now that I have read it...I have to say that I am amazed!<br><br>I mean, when I first started reading this, my rating for the book was like a four and I was only mildly impressed by what I was reading. But then the excitement really picked up. I was actually shocked to be so drawn in by a character in the 3rd person but Violet certainly had mine after the first 50 or so pages. I found her to be quite enjoyable, not one of my favorite YA characters but by far better than most. I am really looking forward to what happens to her in the next book because Derting has left me desperate for more.<br><br>And then of course...there's Jay! *swoon* Now I FINALLY see why the bloggers are all obsessed with this guy! Seriously, how could you not be? He's an actually sweet guy that doesn't seem like a girl dressed in drag. Plus he had his super cute moments, especially when he tried to make her jealous, which is something A LOT of guys do. The only problem I had with him is that I felt Jay lacked character. I would have loved to see more of <i>him</i>, get a greater feel of his personality and that's the only real problem I had with this book. I'm hoping that he develops some life in the sequel.<br><br>And the plot. Holy crap! At first, when I started reading the predators POV, I was pretty skeptical. I kept thinking, 'This is a little dumb' and I kind of laughed at each of the kidnappings (I have a twisted sense of humor). But then I realized just how much of the book was affecting me. It was <i>so</i> wonderfully crafted that my heart would pound and when it was dark, I honestly had to look over my shoulder to see if I was being followed. I couldn't even have the lights off because I was so chilled to the bone by the ending. But the read was well worth it.<br><br>Long story short, I absolutely loved Derting's debut. I can't stop asking myself why why why did I wait so long to read this book and I'm just so excited to get my hands on the sequel, Desires of the Dead, which is out in my bookstore so I'll be getting that in a few weeks. :)<br><br>Rating: 4.9 out of 5 Stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="11014643950188877887" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/93893011" />
    <a title="AH" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3255548-ah"><img alt="AH" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1275413869p2/3255548.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/93893011?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AH" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AH" href="/user/show/3255548-ah">AH</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=zzread-june-2010">zzread-june-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=first-in-series">first-in-series</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer93893011" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12768455770933088034"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6261522.The_Body_Finder__Body_Finder___1_' title='The Body Finder (Body Finder, #1) by Kimberly Derting' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Body Finder</a> is the story of Violet Ambrose. Violet is a normal high school student in every way but one: She can find the imprint of dead people and she can sense people that have had contact with the dead. This gift becomes handy because there is a serial killer on the loose in her town. At a party by the lake, Violet and her best friend Jay find one of the killer's victims in the lake. <br/><br/>Let me say a few words about Jay. Jay is the perfect best friend and later on the perfect boyfriend, prob</span>
  <span id="freeText12768455770933088034" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6261522.The_Body_Finder__Body_Finder___1_" title="The Body Finder (Body Finder, #1) by Kimberly Derting" rel="nofollow noopener">The Body Finder</a> is the story of Violet Ambrose. Violet is a normal high school student in every way but one: She can find the imprint of dead people and she can sense people that have had contact with the dead. This gift becomes handy because there is a serial killer on the loose in her town. At a party by the lake, Violet and her best friend Jay find one of the killer's victims in the lake. <br /><br />Let me say a few words about Jay. Jay is the perfect best friend and later on the perfect boyfriend, probably too perfect to be realistic. He is very attractive and he cares deeply about Violet. Their relationship moves from best friends to boyfriend/girlfriend through the book, with a few annoying hiccups due to the usual miscommunications. <br /><br />The chapters written in the killer's point of view are downright creepy and scary. He thinks like a hunter, referring to himself as the predator and the girls as his prey. <br /><br />There is an underlying sense of danger. The book was well paced and full of suspense. It was hard to put down. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12768455770933088034" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer15321142259979755535">Another great debut to add to the list!<br/><br/>The Body Finder is one of those can't flip the pages fast enough novels. And the point of view chapters from the serial killer added a creep factor like no other ya novel I've read! It was enough to make afraid to be out alone at night...!<br/><br/>I loved the relationship between Jay and Violet. It's so very obvious that they both have feelings for each other and watching their relationship progress was probably my most favorite aspect of the novel. It really balanc</span>
  <span id="freeText15321142259979755535" style="display:none">Another great debut to add to the list!<br /><br />The Body Finder is one of those can't flip the pages fast enough novels. And the point of view chapters from the serial killer added a creep factor like no other ya novel I've read! It was enough to make afraid to be out alone at night...!<br /><br />I loved the relationship between Jay and Violet. It's so very obvious that they both have feelings for each other and watching their relationship progress was probably my most favorite aspect of the novel. It really balances out that whole creepy serial killer part.<br /><br />The Body Finder is just an outstanding read, I can't think of anything that I didn't like. The writing was simplistic, easy to read and entertaining. The characters were realistic and intriguing, and I especially loved the duo of Jay and Violet. The plot was engaging... mysterious and managed to throw in a few plot twists in there I never anticipated.<br /><br />Bottom line... I am a FAN!<br /><br />Looking forward to seeing where Derting takes us in the next installment.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/113204861" />
    <a title="Liza Gilbert" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2035961-liza-gilbert"><img alt="Liza Gilbert" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1482342055p2/2035961.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/113204861?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liza Gilbert" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liza Gilbert" href="/user/show/2035961-liza-gilbert">Liza Gilbert</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2035961-liza-gilbert?shelf=bfya2011">bfya2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2035961-liza-gilbert?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer113204861" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17567099348655146493">I consider the main theme of this book to be Priorities Out of Whack, or Which Story Am I Reading?<br/><br/>Story 1: Violet has the ability to find dead things, especially things or people that have been murdered. When a serial killer strikes and then starts stalking Violet, she must act to save herself and those she loves.<br/><br/>Story 2: Oh. My. God. Jay is Sooooo HAWT! I know he's my bff, but suddenly I want him.<br/><br/>One would rationally think that having a supernatural power and being caught up in string of murder</span>
  <span id="freeText17567099348655146493" style="display:none">I consider the main theme of this book to be Priorities Out of Whack, or Which Story Am I Reading?<br /><br />Story 1: Violet has the ability to find dead things, especially things or people that have been murdered. When a serial killer strikes and then starts stalking Violet, she must act to save herself and those she loves.<br /><br />Story 2: Oh. My. God. Jay is Sooooo HAWT! I know he's my bff, but suddenly I want him.<br /><br />One would rationally think that having a supernatural power and being caught up in string of murders would make your number 1 priority SURVIVAL. In this book, it's whether or not Jay likes Violet, whose car is more fashionable, what her friends are thinking, ad nauseum. It was maddening to read an entire book where the priorities are on making out instead of making it out alive.<br /><br />Plus, would someone PLEASE tell me when authors, especially female authors, are going to stop with the Stephenie Meyer crap about how abusive men are attractive? Example: "She was also shocked by the undisguised fury she saw on Jay's face, but she had to admit that she kind of liked that she could stir such a reaction in him. It meant he cared." - p. 175.<br /><br />To all the ladies and girls out there: No, rage, fury, and violence does not mean he cares about you. It means he's dangerous to be around and you should find somewhere safer to be. According to the National Organization for Women, 4.8 MILLION women are assaulted and/or raped every year by men they are dating or married to. Three women every day are murdered by someone they are dating or married to. Rage does not equal love.<br /><br />I just wish young adult authors would stop glamorizing it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17567099348655146493" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5507588710233861069">This is the first book I read on my Kindle and I enjoyed it immensely. At first I thought the story was pretty predictable, because after a few chapters I was so sure I figured out who the killer was. (I'm such a clever girl *beams*) Turns out I was absolutely wrong, thank god. ^^ <br/><br/>I would have liked to read more about the motive behind the killings. They are explained, but very very briefly. This will make me sound like total wack job but serial killers are interesting people if you look at them</span>
  <span id="freeText5507588710233861069" style="display:none">This is the first book I read on my Kindle and I enjoyed it immensely. At first I thought the story was pretty predictable, because after a few chapters I was so sure I figured out who the killer was. (I'm such a clever girl *beams*) Turns out I was absolutely wrong, thank god. ^^ <br /><br />I would have liked to read more about the motive behind the killings. They are explained, but very very briefly. This will make me sound like total wack job but serial killers are interesting people if you look at them from a purely objective point of view. I can't be the only person on the planet who read up on Jack The Ripper and various other serial killers just because you want to know what makes them tick, what happened to them that led to becoming somebody who craves to torture, to murder, to satisfy their sick needs and to do what they do.<br /><br />I loved the romantic scenes between Jay and Violet, but seriously, how daft and ignorant can a person be? Even one of those banners behind a plane with "JAY LOVES VIOLET" written on it in a bold hot pink letters wouldn't have been enough to make her wake up and smell the lurv (but shoving his tongue down her throat worked pretty well as it turned out)<br /><br />I'm sorry, I'm ranting. Read this book.</span>

<div id="review_751350296" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/751350296" />
    <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please"><img alt="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570038444p2/8422853.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/751350296?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please">Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=unforgettable-male-leads">unforgettable-male-leads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=could-read-over-and-over-again">could-read-over-and-over-again</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer751350296" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3433991293843015965"><b>*4.5 Stars*</b><br/><br/>A quick, fast-paced read that I almost finished in one day. I literally had to slow down so I didn't have two reviews to write in the same day because I was just reading THAT fast. TBF was one of those stories that while it wasn't anything new or groundbreaking, it was fun and took me away from the real world for a bit. It was an escape from reality and it was a change of pace-it came at the perfect time.<br/><br/><b>He reached out, capturing her hand in his. He laced his fingers casually through </b></span>
  <span id="freeText3433991293843015965" style="display:none"><b>*4.5 Stars*</b><br><br>A quick, fast-paced read that I almost finished in one day. I literally had to slow down so I didn't have two reviews to write in the same day because I was just reading THAT fast. TBF was one of those stories that while it wasn't anything new or groundbreaking, it was fun and took me away from the real world for a bit. It was an escape from reality and it was a change of pace-it came at the perfect time.<br><br><b>He reached out, capturing her hand in his. He laced his fingers casually through hers. Violet leaned against him and the calm finally came, settling over her peacefully. And then he kissed her. Gently. Softly. Not on the lips, as she'd imagined so many times before, but on her forehead. The gesture was sweet and a little possessive. <br>Violet hoped, maybe, it was a start.</b><br><br>I've been in two different funks lately-either the books I am reading are SO good that those following don't stand a chance or I've been reading the same old same old and a change of pace is welcoming. Turns out that this time, it was a case of <i>both</i>. I read two or three awesome books in the last week that knocked me off my feet-and while that was refreshing, it also dragged me back into that slump where one of my favorite couples invaded my mind and made it hard to jump into another story (yes, I'm talking Dex and Perry via <i>Ashes to Ashes</i>). I didn't realize it, but I needed a book to pull me away from my favorite ghost hunting duo and back into that happy medium where more than one couple will do, and this book was perfect for the job.<br><br>One of my biggest gripes in books is corny dialogue....and this book was stepping all up in it. BUT, for some reason, and I'm not sure why, I just <i>didn't care</i>. The best part of it is, I didn't have to just cringe and deal with it, it just skirted the issue-it would start something that otherwise normally led to full on unrealistic and forced banter, but it would stop before it got to that point. Not only that, the characters in question of being corny (i.e. the best friends and oh-so-present-enemies) were actually likeable. Yes, likeable. I think that plays a big part in my annoyance most of the time. <br><br>And even more than that, I hate when the author <i>tells us</i> what is happening or going to happen instead of letting it just <i>show</i> in the scene. It's hard to explain, but it's like when the author gives you a play by play of what's going on instead of letting you decipher what it all means and then adding a quote at the end of the explanation in response to what's 'happened'. Probably not the best way to say what I mean, but it's the best I can do. Luckily, I was so engrossed in the story that it didn't seem to matter, and that made me very happy.<br><br>I loved Jay and Violet-I loved that they grew up best friends and did everything together and <b>still</b> did everything together. It made it so adorable when they finally expressed their attraction to one another and only added to the compatibility they clearly already shared. Although, you guessed it, corny, I loved every minute they were together and every minute leading up to it. <br><br>There was suspense, there was jealousy, there was protectiveness, and there were climactic parts that actually had me scanning the pages at lightning speed. I was utterly surprised at the creepy undertone and the idea that young girls were being abdcuted and killed all around our two main characters. It was more than I could have asked for as a filler and I will surprisingly continue this series forward. I <b>can't wait</b> to see what suspense lays ahead of our girl, Violet.<br><br><br><br><br><i>For more of my reviews visit<br><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/" rel="nofollow noopener"><img height="240" width="385" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1407869528i/10772466._SX540_.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a> </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="3433991293843015965" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_70787552" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/70787552" />
    <a title="Crystal" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250501-crystal"><img alt="Crystal" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1378941415p2/2250501.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/70787552?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Crystal" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Crystal" href="/user/show/2250501-crystal">Crystal</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250501-crystal?shelf=2011">2011</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer70787552" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12295638440449777400">WOW! I cannot believe that I waited so long to read this! This is the second book that I have read where the two main love interests have known each other since they were anklebiters and I am loving this concept. Violet and Jay are one of my favorite couples of all time and really I could squee and gush about them forever.<br/>The story is far from simple. Violet ever since she can remember has been able to sense death in a variety of ways. She sees, tastes, or feels an "echo" from a dead body or fro</span>
  <span id="freeText12295638440449777400" style="display:none">WOW! I cannot believe that I waited so long to read this! This is the second book that I have read where the two main love interests have known each other since they were anklebiters and I am loving this concept. Violet and Jay are one of my favorite couples of all time and really I could squee and gush about them forever.<br />The story is far from simple. Violet ever since she can remember has been able to sense death in a variety of ways. She sees, tastes, or feels an "echo" from a dead body or from a predator. I really liked how her family knew about her gift and so did Jay, it wasn't hidden. Sometimes I get tired of reading books where the main gift in the story is secret, this was a nice change for me. Well, Violet feels an echo and when she follows it she finds the body of girl who had been murdered. So the story begins and it is very goosebump worthy. Derting throws in chapters from the killers point of view and every time I read one I wanted to throw the book in the freezer. They were that creepy. I have to also applaud the author because I never saw the twist coming and WOW what a twist it was. I also liked how we got to see Jay and Violet grow together throughout the book. The mystery was great but the love story was just awesome. Did I mention that I really like Jay yet??!!<br />I think everybody should try this book, it has everything imo, murder, mystery, love, and snark what more could you ask for?? I can't wait to read the sequel!! </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2761721729088373827">4.5 stars! <br/><br/>Oh my gosh! <br/><br/>I loved this book, so much. I didn't know what to expect going into this, all I knew was that the blurb had me intrigued. The body finder had everything I look for in a book; a little bit of romance and not only were the main characters amazing and the plot intriguing, but Kimberly Derting's writing style really added to the thrilling side of the novel. <br/><br/>I really enjoyed the romance within the book and liked how it wasn't insta love or rush and how it intertwined with the p</span>
  <span id="freeText2761721729088373827" style="display:none">4.5 stars! <br /><br />Oh my gosh! <br /><br />I loved this book, so much. I didn't know what to expect going into this, all I knew was that the blurb had me intrigued. The body finder had everything I look for in a book; a little bit of romance and not only were the main characters amazing and the plot intriguing, but Kimberly Derting's writing style really added to the thrilling side of the novel. <br /><br />I really enjoyed the romance within the book and liked how it wasn't insta love or rush and how it intertwined with the plot. <br /><br />The plot was really well done and sucked me in from the first page, I mean a girl who can find dead bodies, how amazing and creepy does that sound! The prologue was absolutely outstanding, one of the best I have eve read and just from reading that I was gripped which compelled me to keep reading. I really enjoyed the mystery and liked how Kimberly Derting summed the book up, but I would have liked maybe just a little more suspense towards the ending and whilst finding out hat as actually going on.<br /><br />The way Kimberly Derting wrote the book, especially the mystery parts that kept you on your toes, just added to the suspense feeling, that is created. It wasn't just what Kimberly Derting had written, it was the style in which she had written it, in such a descriptive way that added to the haunting and thrilling aspect of the plot. <br /><br />Overall I really enjoyed this book and am really excited to see how the series progresses through each book. </span>

  <span id="freeText12364023548436100713" style="display:none">This book is a young adult book. I'm in my thirties. Okay, so maybe I'm not giving the book a fair chance. So, I took my 14 year old daughter, and read some of the dialogue between the two main characters (both in their teens). She laughed and said "who in their right mind would ever talk like that". Ok, so maybe it was because I was reading her the dialogue out of context. I don't know. <br /><br />The book seemed like many of the suspense books I read years ago. The "body finder" angle didn't even seem original to me. I guess if you are in your teens, this book would be original because you have nothing to compare it to. I did though.<br /><br />What did I like about it? The cover. I also thought this would be a great book for first time readers (kind of like how Twilight introduced many pre-teens to reading) because its writing is very simple and it would hold the interest for young readers.</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer128604880" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16475677997591790102"><a title='ReadingAfterMidnight' href='http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/kimberly-derling/the-body-finder-review.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380340949i/697215.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Isn't Jay the perfect boyfriend ever? :D <br/><br/>I just LOVED the romance in this book. It felt real for once, you get know why Vi loved Jay - and it was not just a silly crush over his messy hair, or deep eyes or any other thing like that - and you get to love him too for being such a sweet guy. That's because he is so nice to her, always supportive, understanding her (no need for words) and so romantic, and funny.. They are perfect for each other and you get to feel that. For the first time I felt</span>
  <span id="freeText16475677997591790102" style="display:none"><a title="ReadingAfterMidnight" href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/kimberly-derling/the-body-finder-review.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380340949i/697215.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Isn't Jay the perfect boyfriend ever? :D <br><br>I just LOVED the romance in this book. It felt real for once, you get know why Vi loved Jay - and it was not just a silly crush over his messy hair, or deep eyes or any other thing like that - and you get to love him too for being such a sweet guy. That's because he is so nice to her, always supportive, understanding her (no need for words) and so romantic, and funny.. They are perfect for each other and you get to feel that. For the first time I felt in love with a character :)) Some say that he is "to perfect", but from time to time to perfect is just.. perfect :)<br><br>The suspence/mistery part was great too (not so dark anyways) and I liked the chapters from the "hunter"'s perspective. I feel that the action from the ending was not that great (not that much action and a bit rushed), but that's just a little minus in this equation. <br>5 stars already, yeah, it's a great book.<br><br>I just need more, can't wait for the sequel!<br><br>PS: did I say how much I liked Jay? :p<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=goodreads-author">goodreads-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=preston-public-library">preston-public-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=medium-sized">medium-sized</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=suckfest">suckfest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=pretty-covers">pretty-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=its-a-girl">its-a-girl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=2010">2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer95625815" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9888499014555192982">Sixteen year old Violet Ambrose is like any other teenager except she has the ability to sense the murdered. Whether it is a mouse that her cat killed, or the girl she found buried in the woods when she was little, the murdered and the things that killed them are tainted by echoes, which can be sounds, sights, and smells. Despite this morbid ability, Violet has always had the support of her family and her best friend, Jay. But now there is a serial killer loose in town, one that is killing young</span>
  <span id="freeText9888499014555192982" style="display:none">Sixteen year old Violet Ambrose is like any other teenager except she has the ability to sense the murdered. Whether it is a mouse that her cat killed, or the girl she found buried in the woods when she was little, the murdered and the things that killed them are tainted by echoes, which can be sounds, sights, and smells. Despite this morbid ability, Violet has always had the support of her family and her best friend, Jay. But now there is a serial killer loose in town, one that is killing young girls like Violet. Violet realizes that maybe she is the only one who can find and stop him. Things are further complicated by Violet's growing feelings for Jay, who over the summer has become quite a hunk. But Violet doesn't count on the serial killer targeting her. <br /><br />I did not like this book as much as I would have liked to. For a book with such a morbid concept it was surprisingly fluffy. I guess I somehow wanted it to be edgier. People describe this book as being fifty percent romance, fifty percent paranormal, but I think it was more like sixty percent Violent pining over Jay, thirty percent sappiness, and ten percent worrying about actual concerns. It was annoying because it was <i>obvious</i> how the romance was going to play out, but that didn't stop Derting from taking nearly two hundred pages to get there. And the rest of the time was spent with them two making out. The "thriller" part wasn't particular suspenseful because the killer couldn't actually be someone Violet knew, because she would know instantly. And Violet doesn't do much. Things just kind of happen around her. There was one twist I won't spoil. That was it. And the only scene that had me on the edge of my seat was when Violet faces the killer (no surprises there), and even that reaction was stupid in retrospect, because I logically knew everything would turn out all right and there would be a HEA (no surprises there either).<br /><br /><br />So, as you can tell from the mini-rant, this book was a miss for me. I would have liked it if it was edgier, the romance was a subplot, and there to be more action/suspense. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9888499014555192982" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_84706821" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/84706821" />
    <a title="Elizabeth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1762033-elizabeth"><img alt="Elizabeth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1491327487p2/1762033.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/84706821?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elizabeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elizabeth" href="/user/show/1762033-elizabeth">Elizabeth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer84706821" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1308352879707985039"><b>RULES TO LIVE BY:</b><br/>1.) Do not sprain your ankle when there is a killer on the loose and he has pegged you as his next victim.<br/>2.) Do not go into an empty washroom located in a dark, abandoned hallway when there is a killer on the loose and he has pegged you as his next victim.<br/>3.) If your boyfriend pins you down and forces you to tell him you love him, you may want to re-evaluate your relationship with him.<br/>4.) If your friends lead you towards an empty washroom located in a dark, abandoned hallway wh</span>
  <span id="freeText1308352879707985039" style="display:none"><b>RULES TO LIVE BY:</b><br />1.) Do not sprain your ankle when there is a killer on the loose and he has pegged you as his next victim.<br />2.) Do not go into an empty washroom located in a dark, abandoned hallway when there is a killer on the loose and he has pegged you as his next victim.<br />3.) If your boyfriend pins you down and forces you to tell him you love him, you may want to re-evaluate your relationship with him.<br />4.) If your friends lead you towards an empty washroom located in a dark, abandoned hallway when there is a killer on the loose and he has pegged you as his next victim, you may want to re-evaluate your relationship with them.<br />5.) And finally, if you choose to stay alone in an empty washroom located in a dark, abandoned hallway when there is a killer on the loose and he has pegged you as your next victim, you may want to re-evaluate your whole life because you are clearly an idiot and for some reason nobody has noticed.<br /><br />This was Twilight with serial killers instead of vampires. Violet was a less annoying version of Bella and Jay was a scarier, more possessive version of Edward. But otherwise it was the same book: two mildly (MILDLY) interesting characters that caused the book to turn to crap in my hands the second they fell in grade eleven love with each other. <br /><br />Violet became completely dependent on Jay and was only happy when he was around. Jay became intensely overprotective and obsessive, literally only leaving Violet's side to use the bathroom or go to sleep at night (if he wasn't human I'm positive he would have sat up all night and watched her sleep just like Eddie). And then Violet almost got herself killed because she made the dumbest decision in the entire world that no one would ever, ever make if they knew there was a serial killer after them. GOSH.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1308352879707985039" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!

    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('UP6aVLJjJ1RYdrJEt6mnzAy/qA1UiFTjnbgcno5VEO5q2POGCT3uPP9dBiVAXK0T2uBPxZoF2oTGxlovQxbidA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3nyzZcyytCtzIckp1hm86dpdITNWdWSHZ+547jy2jDXkWtq3d+x9Q9QKfUgh7LY2DALG+5j46uA8kD5f8fV+rw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

  <span id="freeText7110914906564175695" style="display:none">Kimberly is the author of the award-winning THE BODY FINDER series, THE PLEDGE, and THE TAKING trilogies.
